## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillations / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the equation of motion (acceleration) for a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration dv_dt is determined by restoring forces (dependent on x), damping forces (dependent on v), and possibly time-dependent driving forces, with nonlinear terms distinguishing it from the simple harmonic case.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (external periodic drive)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear restoring)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Softening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (quadratic asymmetric nonlinearity)
- General polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric + symmetric nonlinearity)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (quadratic drag)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-varying stiffness)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve oscillation symmetry; even powers (x**2) break it â€” check symmetry in data
- Negative linear stiffness with positive cubic (c0*x + c1*x**3 where c0>0, c1<0 or vice versa) indicates double-well or hardening/softening spring behavior
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v indicate energy dissipation or injection; sign determines damping vs. self-excitation
- Products of x**2 and v (like x**2*v) are hallmarks of van der Pol-type nonlinear damping with amplitude-dependent energy exchange
- Explicit time dependence through trigonometric functions sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicates external periodic forcing/driving
- If dv_dt depends only on x and v (no explicit t), the system is autonomous and phase-plane analysis applies
- Rational terms like x/(1 + c*x**2) can model saturating restoring forces that plateau at large displacements
- Mixed terms like x*v indicate velocity-dependent modification of the restoring force, common in gyroscopic or Coriolis-type effects

Let me analyze the candidates systematically. Most candidates use polynomial terms in x (like `x`, `x**3`, `x**c`), rational functions `x/(c+xآ²)`, or other basis functions. None of these can exactly equal `x*exp(-|x|)`.

**Key observations:**
- `x*exp(-|x|)` cannot be represented by any polynomial, rational function, `sin`, `cos`, `log`, or power function `x**c` for any fixed c.
- A sum of power functions `x**c` with different exponents cannot equal `x*exp(-|x|)` because `exp(-|x|)` is not a power of |x|.
- Rational functions like `x/(c+xآ²)` cannot equal `x*exp(-|x|)` either.
- `log(c*x+1)` terms cannot produce `x*exp(-|x|)`.
- `sin` and `cos` terms cannot produce `x*exp(-|x|)`.

Since `x*exp(-|x|)` is a transcendental function that is linearly independent from all polynomials, rational functions, power functions, logarithms, and trigonometric functions, **no candidate that lacks an explicit `exp` term can match the GT**.

Let me verify: none of the 50 candidates contain `exp(...)` in their expressions. They all use combinations of:
- Polynomials in x (`x`, `x**2`, `x**3`, `x**4`, `x**5`)
- Power functions (`x**c`)
- Rational functions (`.../(c+xآ²)`)
- `log(c*x+1)`
- `sin(...)`, `cos(...)`
- `v`, `v*x**2`, `v*x**4`
- `t` terms

None of these basis functions can produce `x*exp(-|x|)`. Therefore, no candidate can exactly match the GT.
